English (MT)

In his own body, (i.e.,) in the sky of consciousness, like the ocean of milk, from the conjunction and disjunction of the waves of his own sakti-s,
he emits the and destroys this universe.

English (MT)

This indeed is the light.
In his own body - in his own form; in the sky of consciousness тАУ like on a wall formed by undifferentiated consciousness;
from the conjunction and disjunction of the waves of his own sakti-s тАУ from the conjunction of the his own rays of the form of Khecari and the like.
By projecting them for the sake of cognition of specific objects, he emits, i.e., he manifests the universe starting from Siva тАУ
and by the disjunction - by drawing away cognition of [specific object] he causes destruction, i.e., dissolution of the world] -
just as the conjunction of ocean waves generates billows, bubbles and the like and their disjunction cause these to dissolve.

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН - рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

It may be understood as:
Consciousness (cit = the bhairava) should be contemplated as possessed of innumerable wheels-within-wheels of his own shakti-s emanating this universe, pervading the five sensory fields, and assuming the forms of experienced objects, senses and the experiencer.

This metaphor of the wheels within wheels has always appealed to us, as we have seen it as a fractal analogy that triggers something primal in the brain and beyond.
